Timmy didn't understand why he should bury it, but his mom explained that it was a way to show respect for things we care about.Timmy felt bad for not taking care of his toy car and promised to tidy up his toys from now on. The moral of the story is that we should take care of our things and show respect for them, even if they are broken.

Original Story: Once upon a time, there were two friends, Daisy and Tom. Daisy had a pretty bow in her hair, and Tom had a smile on his face. They were walking in the woods one day when something strange happened. They suddenly heard a whisper coming from behind a tree. "Come here," it said. Feeling a bit scared, Daisy and Tom peeked around the tree. They saw an owl perched on a branch. He had big, wise eyes and a soft voice. He told the pair that there was an important mission that needed their help.The owl asked them to take the bow from Daisy's hair and tie it to the branch of the tree. Here is your cat paper. You can keep it." She gives him the cat paper.Ben says, "Thank you, boss. You are very nice. Can we play something else now?" Lily says, "Yes, we can. Let's play doctor. I will be the doctor and you will be the patient." They put away the office things and take out some toys. They laugh and play together. They have a lot of fun.

They will always be remembered as two friends in love with the warmth of the sun.

Original Story: Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. One day, she was very hot and wanted some cold water. She went to the kitchen and opened the refrigerator. Her mommy smiled and said, "Yes, the refrigerator makes things cold." Lily's mommy then gave her a warm blanket to cover herself. Lily felt much better and snuggled under the blanket. She was happy that the fierce heat was gone and she was feeling warm again.

Mummy smiled. "You're very welcome, little one," she said.

She had been right all along- he was the same delivery man she always got her presents from.

She says they have to stay after school. She says they have to do the work again. And they have to do more work. And they have to say sorry.Tom and Sue are very sad. They wish they had searched for words. They wish they had not been silly. They wish they could play in the park. But they have to stay in school. They have to do the work. They have to listen to Miss Lee. They have to be good. They learn their lesson.

You should go home now."The little girl understood and eventually went home. From that day on, she was always careful when she was outside.The moral of the story is that being careless can be dangerous. We should always be alert and cautious when we are out and about.

She thanked the Wind King, and he flew away.

As he was swimming up, he saw something that made him hesitate - a tall and long wall that seemed to stretch on forever!Ollie was feeling discouraged and didn't know if he should turn back. Then, he heard a voice from above. It was a dolphin who was swimming beside the wall. "Hey Ollie!" the dolphin said, "You can do it. Just zip up the wall and you'll be out of the ocean in no time!" The octopus was feeling a bit anxious, but with a determined and enthusiastic attitude, Ollie decided to take the dolphin's advice. He zoomed up the wall with the help of his tentacles and, to his surprise, he made it to the top.The moral of the story is that it is important to stay enthusiastic and never give up, even when the obstacles seem impossible to overcome!
Original Summary: Octopus Ollie ventured out of the ocean to explore the world above, but was discouraged by a tall and long wall that seemed to stretch on forever. With the encouragement of a dolphin, Ollie decided to take a chance and zip up the wall, successfully reaching the top and learning the importance of staying enthusiastic and never giving up.

Joe felt much better and stopped crying. His mom had a kind and gentle voice, and it made Joe feel safe.His mom sat down with Joe and explained to him what the "law" was. She said it was there to protect and comfort people, like her and Joe. She said it was important to always follow the law, because it was there to keep people safe. Joe understood and felt a lot better. His mom had made him feel comforted with her kind words. He knew he could always count on his mom to take care of him.
Original Summary: Joe, a three-year-old boy, was playing in the park when he became scared and confused after something bad happened. His mother, who had a kind and gentle voice, comforted him and explained the importance of following the law to keep people safe.

He squatted down and gazed into the deep blue water. Once again, he yawned, this time in content. Suddenly, he heard a noise coming from the bushes. Davey was a bit scared, but he was also brave. He stood up and turned around, and to his amazement, he saw a small deer staring straight at him. Davey smiled, and after a while, the deer let out a loud yawn before it trotted off into the woods.Davey laughed, waved goodbye to the deer and continued exploring the forest. Every so often he would stop, yawn and take a deep breath of the herbal air. He knew he would never forget this special day out in the forest.

Original Story: Once upon a time, there lived a little girl named Lucy. She had a pet goldfish called Timmy. Every day, Lucy would take care of Timmy, feeding him and talking to him. One day she decided to take him to the beach.At the beach Lucy saw something shiny under the water. It was an oyster! She was so excited. She quickly scooped up the oyster with her hands and brought it to shore.When Lucy opened up the oyster, she found a sparkly pearl inside. She couldn't believe it! She was so excited she started jumping up and down.But then, Lucy felt somebody tap her shoulder. It was an old fisherman! He said to her, "That oyster was hurt by your little goldfish here." He pointed to Timmy in Lucy's bucket.Lucy felt so sad. She said sorry to the old fisherman and promised to pour some water over the oyster so it could go back safely to the ocean. "Thank you," said the old fisherman with a smile. So, Lucy carefully poured the water on the oyster, and it slowly slid away into the waves.Lucy and Timmy went back home together that day with a very important lesson.

The bird ate the crumbs and looked at Lily with grateful eyes.Lily felt happy that she could help the bird. She learned that even though she was small, she could make a big difference. She also learned that sometimes, helping others might make us feel a little fearful, but it's important to be brave and do the right thing. From that day on, Lily always looked out for the animals in her garden and helped them whenever she could.
